  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_07587d11-9b8e-4897-bd85-7c387196198a'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer2048969468001254354">On a moonless night, two rats follow hypnotic lights into the forest, never to be seen again. Such is the power of the Doomwytes, sinister ravens led by the deadly Korvus Skurr. And when the young mouse Bisky persuades the creatures of Redwall Abbey to go in search of a fabled treasure, hidden long ago by one of the abbey's most notorious thieves, they do not suspect Skurr</span>
  <span id="freeText2048969468001254354" style="display:none">On a moonless night, two rats follow hypnotic lights into the forest, never to be seen again. Such is the power of the Doomwytes, sinister ravens led by the deadly Korvus Skurr. And when the young mouse Bisky persuades the creatures of Redwall Abbey to go in search of a fabled treasure, hidden long ago by one of the abbey's most notorious thieves, they do not suspect Skurr and his ravens will be vying for that very treasure. Bisky and his fellow Redwallers must summon all their courage to face the evil horde of slithering snakes and vicious ravens. From underground tunnels to the tops of trees, the fearless Redwallers, with the help of their woodland friends, battle some of their most vicious enemies yet in an exhilarating, terrifying treasure hunt.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1914762796" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1914762796" />
    <a title="Josiah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1914201-josiah"><img alt="Josiah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1239682454p2/1914201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1914762796?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josiah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josiah" href="/user/show/1914201-josiah">Josiah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1914762796" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7101987993545180843"><i>Doomwyte</i> is the twentieth full-length novel of the Redwall saga, but Brian Jacques wasn't the only original member of the series' creative team still onboard at that point: Troy Howell did the cover art for <i>Doomwyte</i> and every Redwall novel preceding it, and his skill showed not a whit of decline after twenty-two years. Brian Jacques introduces some new elements in <i>Doomwyte</i>, while maintaining the standby motifs that fans of the series love. As Redwallers Dwink (a young squirrel), Bisky (a mouse o</span>
  <span id="freeText7101987993545180843" style="display:none"><i>Doomwyte</i> is the twentieth full-length novel of the Redwall saga, but Brian Jacques wasn't the only original member of the series' creative team still onboard at that point: Troy Howell did the cover art for <i>Doomwyte</i> and every Redwall novel preceding it, and his skill showed not a whit of decline after twenty-two years. Brian Jacques introduces some new elements in <i>Doomwyte</i>, while maintaining the standby motifs that fans of the series love. As Redwallers Dwink (a young squirrel), Bisky (a mouse of the same age), and Dugry (a mole) discover there's truth behind the legend of a priceless treasure swiped by Gonff the Mousethief untold seasons ago, an evil gathering of carrion birds lurks in an underground grotto of Mossflower Wood, hoping to steal the treasure for themselves. The birds are led by a violent-tempered raven called Korvus Skurr, who depends on a serpent seer to divine what future course the birds should take. Korvus covets the legendary jewels of Gonff to complete his own collection and earn him great prestige in Mossflower and beyond, and he's not afraid to launch an attack on Redwall Abbey if that's what it comes to. A war unlike any in the Abbey's history could be at hand. <br /><br /> The discovery of Gonff's book of riddles puts the Redwallers on the trail of Gonff's jewels, a trail that leads beyond the Abbey walls. As the quest progresses, Korvus enlists the terrifying adder Baliss to lay siege to Redwall and pressure the young treasure seekers into giving up, but Korvus's authority among his own birds is already disintegrating, and the plan immediately goes wrong. Soon Baliss shows up at Korvus's underground lair to make trouble for the raven who hired him while Bisky, Dwink, and their party of finders pursue the treasure unhindered. It will be a proud homecoming for the young ones if they return to the Abbey with Gonff's jewels, but the elders will be just as proud to see how they have matured during these troubling times. In the face of enemies as frightening as any faced by past Redwall warriors, this generation has made its mark and proven their worth. The Abbey will be in good hands for many seasons to come. <br /><br /> I was intrigued by a few story components of <i>Doomwyte</i>, components that undoubtedly would have better served the series when it was newer and more spry. Well-worn plot devices are avoided for the most part in these pages, and the characters show promise. Brother Torilis? Baliss? Laird Bosie McScutta of Bowlaynee, heir to the mantle of eccentric warrior hares? They would be invaluable assets to earlier Redwall novels, probably written more cleverly and leveraged for major emotional payoffs in the story. Redwall in its prime is a spectacular series, and its halcyon days are a literary marvel. They are the legacy of Brian Jacques. <br /><br /> "Homecomings can be coloured by many emotions."<br /><br /> —<i>Doomwyte</i>, P. 363<br /><br /> <i>Doomwyte</i> is the least exceptional of the first twenty Redwall books, but there's a quote here or there worth remembering. I'd give it one and a half stars, and the epilogue was nearly enough for me to consider rounding up to two. If you've made it this far in the series, you know before starting <i>Doomwyte</i> that it isn't likely to be another <i>Mattimeo</i>, <i>Martin the Warrior</i>, or <i>The Bellmaker</i>, but it's nostalgic fun for those who have loved passing time in this fantasy world for most of their lives. There's no substitution for a few days spent in the land of Redwall, and I hope readers always feel that way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7101987993545180843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_185007079" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185007079" />
    <a title="Ryan Handermann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2574265-ryan-handermann"><img alt="Ryan Handermann" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185007079?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan Handermann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan Handermann" href="/user/show/2574265-ryan-handermann">Ryan Handermann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101157992" href="/book/show/9045960-doomwyte">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2574265-ryan-handermann?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185007079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3142517795384613065">I picked the audiobook up at the Library. I loved the Redwall books as a middle-schooler, so mostly I picked this up to see if my tastes back then were any good. I can see why I liked them. They are very well crafted stories, easy to follow, but have a lot of fun and "exciting" twists and turns. Mostly Brian Jacques sticks to a very narrow story pattern which is repeated in every book. This isn't all bad, he does it well and so its perhaps good that he sticks with what he knows.<br/><br/>The biggest criti</span>
  <span id="freeText3142517795384613065" style="display:none">I picked the audiobook up at the Library. I loved the Redwall books as a middle-schooler, so mostly I picked this up to see if my tastes back then were any good. I can see why I liked them. They are very well crafted stories, easy to follow, but have a lot of fun and "exciting" twists and turns. Mostly Brian Jacques sticks to a very narrow story pattern which is repeated in every book. This isn't all bad, he does it well and so its perhaps good that he sticks with what he knows.<br /><br />The biggest criticism of these books I have is that they are racist. It is fantasy after all and set in a different world with different rules so maybe its okay to be racist when dealing with animals. When I say racist, I mean that race defines if you are good and bad, and you cannot change that - you are born that way. Thus, mice, rabbits, etc. are basically good. This is actually kind of a strange concept for me. Imagine a people who have the inability to perform evil, or at least, great evil. They do make small mistakes, but they simply cannot do really bad things. A mouse could never kill another mouse. Rats, on the other hand, have the inability to actually be good and do great good. Again, they can slip up for a bit and do some good things, even join the Abbey for a bit like in Outcast of Redwall, but they cannot fully embrace good.<br /><br />If this "anthropology" (or rodentology)were actually true, our stories would be much different. In the Bible, there are distinctions between the righteous and the wicked, but they are more fluid. Wicked can become righteous, and righteous can become wicked. Israel as a whole is the most obvious example. They start out as God's chosen people - you don't get more righteous than that. Then, they kill the son of God and God rejects that race in favor of another race - the gentiles. Or, on a more individual level, we could take Abraham. A righteous man, yet, he doesn't seem to mind prostituting his wife with Pharaoh. Or take Aaron. He is the mouthpiece of Moses and high priest - and then builds a golden calf (or did that just pop out of the fire?). Or take Moses. The most humble man in the world, but he still gets angry and hits the rock really hard.<br /><br />The Bible has a much more nuanced picture of the good guys and the bad guys than the Redwall stories. One might say that the Redwall stories are for kids, so its good to simplify things for them. That is true, as long as the simplifications do not distort the truth. We can teach our kids that Abraham was righteous, that Moses was awesome, that David was a great. And that Cain was evil, and Manassah was horrible, and that Ham was cursed. This is all true. But there are other stories where Abraham was stupid, Moses was disobedient, and David was sinful. In Redwall, these other stories do not exist. Given that there are now 20 books in this series and that each book is considerably large, they are too big to be over-simplified. I think that this defect creates a false view of reality.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3142517795384613065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/1242515-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1242515-hannah?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96484334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1727199153880446268">Many people have complained that Brian Jacques has been churning out the same book over and over and simply replacing the characters and villain - I've seen complaints along these lines since way back with The Long Patrol! I've never felt it until now, but I think at this point in the series, it's definitely feeling rehashed.<br/><br/>This time, the villains are carion birds of all types (as well as an adder), and the hero is... a mouse? I think he's a descendent of Gonff or something, but I've forgotten </span>
  <span id="freeText1727199153880446268" style="display:none">Many people have complained that Brian Jacques has been churning out the same book over and over and simply replacing the characters and villain - I've seen complaints along these lines since way back with The Long Patrol! I've never felt it until now, but I think at this point in the series, it's definitely feeling rehashed.<br /><br />This time, the villains are carion birds of all types (as well as an adder), and the hero is... a mouse? I think he's a descendent of Gonff or something, but I've forgotten already. That's probably not a good sign. As usual, there's a lone warrior, a hare that pops up just when he's needed and provides much needed military assistance, and the bad guys are defeated.<br /><br />For first time readers of the Redwall series, I'd definitely recommend other books in the series. Anything pre-Triss was pretty good, but afterwards they've started feeling a little dull. Huge fans of Redwall like me will probably read it anyway and at least enjoy the sentimental value, though I wouldn't recommend expecting a lot out of it. Jacques' books are so lovely and I've enjoyed most of them so much in the past that I find this problem easily forgiven and forgotten, however. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1727199153880446268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11883020768741548282">I love the Redwall series. It's always fun to dip into the Mossflower Woods and spend some time with the mice, shrews, hares and otters of the Redwall Abbey, and to read some exciting battle scenes with the "vermin" characters of rats, snakes, ravens, and so forth. I listened to this full cast audio recording and boy was it entertaining. The author narrates, in his loovly Liverpudlian accent, and the actors who play all the parts all have the right accents for the moles and other animals. Plus t</span>
  <span id="freeText11883020768741548282" style="display:none">I love the Redwall series. It's always fun to dip into the Mossflower Woods and spend some time with the mice, shrews, hares and otters of the Redwall Abbey, and to read some exciting battle scenes with the "vermin" characters of rats, snakes, ravens, and so forth. I listened to this full cast audio recording and boy was it entertaining. The author narrates, in his loovly Liverpudlian accent, and the actors who play all the parts all have the right accents for the moles and other animals. Plus there are songs sung, which really adds to the character. In this volume, Redwall mouse Bisky and squirrel Dwink get caught up in a quest for rubies and emeralds (the stolen eyes of the Doomwyte statue), while the evil Korvus Skurr, raven leader of the Wytes gang, also seeks the gems--and he's got a giant nasty serpent to help him! (shiver)</span>

<div id="review_39971337" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39971337" />
    <a title="Samuel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1107224-samuel"><img alt="Samuel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1209776302p2/1107224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Redwall fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3089516-courtney-pirogoeth?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3089516-courtney-pirogoeth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83462195" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1082567998550768555">I just finished Doomwyte, the twentieth book in the Redwall series. Right now it’s the only one I don’t own. Obviously I love the series. Every book follows a simliar formula, but is always a great story.<br/><br/>This time the Redwallers and the evil don’t have much to do with each other for a while. Korvus Skurr, leader of the Doomwytes, wants to restore the eyes to the Doomwyte idol and lead his flock of carrion birds into a great new age. A passing bird evesdrops and hears a story told by a young Redw</span>
  <span id="freeText1082567998550768555" style="display:none">I just finished Doomwyte, the twentieth book in the Redwall series. Right now it’s the only one I don’t own. Obviously I love the series. Every book follows a simliar formula, but is always a great story.<br /><br />This time the Redwallers and the evil don’t have much to do with each other for a while. Korvus Skurr, leader of the Doomwytes, wants to restore the eyes to the Doomwyte idol and lead his flock of carrion birds into a great new age. A passing bird evesdrops and hears a story told by a young Redwaller, Bisky, regarding the jewel eyes. This starts everything into motion.<br />Skurr tries to find out information by trying to have a Redwaller kidnapped. The stupid birds try to take a Dibbun (basically a toddler) who wouldn’t know anything of the story. Without knowing that someone else is interested in the jewels, a small group starts to work on finding them. From there more adventures ensue, friends and enemies are met, and finally the final confrontation occurs with… no, I won’t spill the ending. ;)<br /><br />It is a wonderful book as usual. It’s interesting to see how many little changes have occured over the series. For a while there was at least one character that was around in the previous book. Now we’re lucky to get a name mentioned in passing. This one deals with a character from way back in the beginning of the history of Redwall Abbey. Other little differences are there, but make sense as many seasons have passed since the first Redwall book was written. It’s still as good as ever and I am really looking forward to the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1082567998550768555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1155636946?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth" href="/user/show/31967709-elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31967709-elizabeth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31967709-elizabeth?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1155636946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16420384099803158015">(mild spoilers)<br/><br/>This book is a refreshing one in the Redwall series in terms of plot elements (Redwall recycles plot elements like crazy): some of the Fetch Quest Items were outside the Abbey, rather than hidden inside; the villain and his cronies were fairly unique; and Tugga Bruster was a mean and nasty Log a Log that nobody really mourned. I wish Balis hadn’t been given the Mad Villain Treatment so early on, but the threat he made even going mad was at least legitimate unlike Korvus Skurr, who</span>
  <span id="freeText16420384099803158015" style="display:none">(mild spoilers)<br /><br />This book is a refreshing one in the Redwall series in terms of plot elements (Redwall recycles plot elements like crazy): some of the Fetch Quest Items were outside the Abbey, rather than hidden inside; the villain and his cronies were fairly unique; and Tugga Bruster was a mean and nasty Log a Log that nobody really mourned. I wish Balis hadn’t been given the Mad Villain Treatment so early on, but the threat he made even going mad was at least legitimate unlike Korvus Skurr, who didn’t actually do much besides throw snakes to the catfish.<br /><br />I do think the Redwall books with one main hero and his/her sidekick are better than the group hero books because the former can focus more on development. Bisky and the others (I can’t even remember their names) were pretty flat and even Bosie, who carried the Sword of Martin, was forgettable. I did like Zaran, though, because even though she filled the “warrior wants revenge” trope, I did think she was quite sweet (as in charming) as a whole, and she managed to put the past behind her and move on with a new life.<br /><br />Also, I did like the inclusion of the Gonfelins, even though we’ve never heard of them before, and some of the new places found in the Abbey. This book was heavy on exploring for much of it, and I enjoy exploring.<br /><br />Read more Redwall reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://leafsreviews.wordpress.com/">http://leafsreviews.wordpress.com/</a></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107214761" />
    <a title="Anki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3080902-anki"><img alt="Anki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559670780p2/3080902.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107214761?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anki" href="/user/show/3080902-anki">Anki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3080902-anki?shelf=status-own">status-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3080902-anki?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3080902-anki?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107214761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14183840455225264389">This latest installment of the Redwall series strikes a wonderful balance between classic Redwall adventures and something new, which is essential for part of a long-running series. Like most of the recent books, <i>Doomwyte</i> is set an unspecified number of seasons after the events in <i>Redwall</i>, but as near as I can tell before the books and records were moved from the Gatehouse into the library in <i>High Rhulain</i>.<br/><br/>The story itself stays pretty tightly focused on the Abbey and its surroundings, which is a</span>
  <span id="freeText14183840455225264389" style="display:none">This latest installment of the Redwall series strikes a wonderful balance between classic Redwall adventures and something new, which is essential for part of a long-running series. Like most of the recent books, <i>Doomwyte</i> is set an unspecified number of seasons after the events in <i>Redwall</i>, but as near as I can tell before the books and records were moved from the Gatehouse into the library in <i>High Rhulain</i>.<br /><br />The story itself stays pretty tightly focused on the Abbey and its surroundings, which is a change from many of the other books in the series which range from the northlands to far-flung islands and the great mountain Salamandastron on the shores of the sea. I enjoy both types of stories, and I am very happy to see that Brian Jacques can tell both equally well.<br /><br /><i>Doomwyte</i> also draws more heavily on spooky and supernatural elements than most of the other Redwall novels, and I quite enjoyed that difference.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14183840455225264389" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/368999-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1196973969p2/368999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/368999-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Brian Jacques fans</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39131054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10068145017956103413"><i>Doomwyte</i> is the most recent book by Brian Jacques featuring the creatures of Redwall. I was a little disappointed by this one. There were still the wonderful descriptions of Redwall Abbey and all the feasts and the different animal dialects, but the story was just not very convincing. It seems like maybe the last 2 or 3 of his books didn't have as strong of a storyline as most of his earlier books did. I guess there are only so many ways that Redwall Abbey and/or it's inhabitants can be attacked</span>
  <span id="freeText10068145017956103413" style="display:none"><i>Doomwyte</i> is the most recent book by Brian Jacques featuring the creatures of Redwall. I was a little disappointed by this one. There were still the wonderful descriptions of Redwall Abbey and all the feasts and the different animal dialects, but the story was just not very convincing. It seems like maybe the last 2 or 3 of his books didn't have as strong of a storyline as most of his earlier books did. I guess there are only so many ways that Redwall Abbey and/or it's inhabitants can be attacked by various "vermin". Overall, though still a typical Redwall book - full of interesting animals having adventures.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10068145017956103413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1415219135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1415219135" />
    <a title="Kelsey Hanson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14303907-kelsey-hanson"><img alt="Kelsey Hanson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353034986p2/14303907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1415219135?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelsey Hanson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelsey Hanson" href="/user/show/14303907-kelsey-hanson">Kelsey Hanson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1415219135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2474974089976378512">Like I say in every single Redwall book I've ever reviewed, I love the series so this is not going to be an entirely biased reviewer and this series is my go-to book series after I've read something really frustrating (in this case way too many Tamora Pierce books). I've actually been dragging my heels about reading the last couple of books in the series. Not because I'm afraid they will be bad, but Jacques died in 2011 and even though I'm a fully grown adult it makes me sad that there will be n</span>
  <span id="freeText2474974089976378512" style="display:none">Like I say in every single Redwall book I've ever reviewed, I love the series so this is not going to be an entirely biased reviewer and this series is my go-to book series after I've read something really frustrating (in this case way too many Tamora Pierce books). I've actually been dragging my heels about reading the last couple of books in the series. Not because I'm afraid they will be bad, but Jacques died in 2011 and even though I'm a fully grown adult it makes me sad that there will be no new Redwall books.<br /><br />That being said, I love this series, but I'm not too close to the books not to see some of the problems. A common argument against this series is that they are formulaic and predictable. I don't disagree with that though I do make the argument that the books have enough personality and Jacques was such a good storyteller who clearly loved to tell these stories that I've always found them very entertaining. This one, however, has many of the familiar motifs, but they never really come together like they had in previous books. In fact, this might be my least favorite Redwall book to date. The plot was kinda all over the place and the villain was pretty forgettable (and a tad confusing honestly). Also, what normally happens in the series is that the focus is divided between a group goes questing away from the abbey (usually at sea somehow) and then the group that stays at the abbey. This one stayed pretty close to Mossflower for the entirety and honestly I found myself missing the searats a bit if for no other reason they are usually pretty interesting villains/comic relief characters. <br /><br />*Spoilers ahead* <br /><br />That being said, there was still quite a few things that I like about this series. This is the first book in the series that I can recall that ends with a married abbess with children which answers a question I've had for years about whether that was allowed or not. I also always like that Jacques is always pretty varied with the types of characters he features. There's always a mix of old and young and male and female and in a variety of roles. Women are portrayed as leaders and warriors while men are portrayed as healers, cooks and gardeners and vice versa without any gender expectations. This happens again with the character of Torilis who is a curmudgeon with a very caring side. I also liked that Gonff has such a legacy. He is one of my favorite recurring characters and it's always great to hear about him again.<br /><br />Not my favorite, far from it actually, but still a Redwall book so worth a read! </span>
  <a data-text-id="2474974089976378512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2207152583" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2207152583" />
    <a title="Addyson Huneke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74443790-addyson-huneke"><img alt="Addyson Huneke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545673224p2/74443790.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2207152583?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Addyson Huneke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Addyson Huneke" href="/user/show/74443790-addyson-huneke">Addyson Huneke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2207152583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3568238888435522870">Just be forewarned, I'm trying to watch a football game while I'm writing this, so if this review is incoherent, I'm sorry. But the Falcons are playing the Colts right now. <br/><br/>So, on to the review! This is my first venture into the Redwall world. A friend at church talked about Redwall enough she convinced me to try one out, and while I enjoyed the book, I'm not sure if I'll take another venture in.<br/><br/>Writing: 3.75/5<br/>The writing, while pretty good, wasn't as good as it could have been. It seemed as Bri</span>
  <span id="freeText3568238888435522870" style="display:none">Just be forewarned, I'm trying to watch a football game while I'm writing this, so if this review is incoherent, I'm sorry. But the Falcons are playing the Colts right now. <br /><br />So, on to the review! This is my first venture into the Redwall world. A friend at church talked about Redwall enough she convinced me to try one out, and while I enjoyed the book, I'm not sure if I'll take another venture in.<br /><br />Writing: 3.75/5<br />The writing, while pretty good, wasn't as good as it could have been. It seemed as Brian Jacques was semi-trying to write deep POV. He didn't pull it off very well. And there was a really annoying quirk that pulled me out of the writing more than once where he would blend two sentences together with just a comma which should have been replaced by a period. Gah, grammar issues. I tried to overlook it and enjoy the story. Other than that, it was fairly well-written, just not spectacular.<br /><br />Setting: 4.5/5<br />It wasn't spectacular. I couldn't really tell if it was supposed to be in a separate world from the text, although my friend at church assured me so (I think). Other than that, it seemed pretty good, just nothing stood out.<br /><br />Plot: 4/5<br />Well? You've seen me say before I couldn't pinpoint the plot, but I loved it. I sort of pinpointed the plot, it just wasn't a very dynamic or moving one. There wasn't even a reason to be searching for the lost Great Eyes of the Doomwyte other than the adventure, and there was absolutely no clear idea what they were going to do with them when they acquired them all! SPOILERS When they got them, all they did was rebury them, which was...a huge anticlimax, to say the least. SPOILERS They ran into trouble and everything, so there was excitement, or it would have been, if I had been more invested in the characters, but I'll get to that in the next section.<br /><br />Character Development: 3.5/5<br />I know why I didn't connect with the characters well. There was no clear protagonist. I'm serious! There was no protagonist. There characters were fairly well-developed, but there was no clear main character. The characters were a little more two-dimensional than three-dimensional, but they were well enough developed that I was invested enough to keep reading.<br /><br />In review, I think I would have enjoyed this book a lot more if I had been younger. It was definitely an adventure story for a younger reader, although it has a more mature tone. I don't know, maybe being a writer has made me more picky about stories, but I'm not sure if I enjoyed it enough to read more of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3568238888435522870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2073186113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2073186113" />
    <a title="Jeremy Michael Gallen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35009294-jeremy-michael-gallen"><img alt="Jeremy Michael Gallen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535388215p2/35009294.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2073186113?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeremy Michael Gallen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeremy Michael Gallen" href="/user/show/35009294-jeremy-michael-gallen">Jeremy Michael Gallen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2073186113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10541106933928877581">In the twentieth of the late Brian Jacques’ Redwall series, which he dedicates to a “true warrior,” Private First-Class Donald Reas Axtell, the residents of the series’ eponymous Abbey face formidable adversaries in a hunt for lost treasure. The book features a brief but somewhat confounding prologue of days supposedly no longer warm, although this is somewhat contradictory since spring and summer are the chief seasons of the story. In the main chapters, a magpie named Griv seeks shelter from st</span>
  <span id="freeText10541106933928877581" style="display:none">In the twentieth of the late Brian Jacques’ Redwall series, which he dedicates to a “true warrior,” Private First-Class Donald Reas Axtell, the residents of the series’ eponymous Abbey face formidable adversaries in a hunt for lost treasure. The book features a brief but somewhat confounding prologue of days supposedly no longer warm, although this is somewhat contradictory since spring and summer are the chief seasons of the story. In the main chapters, a magpie named Griv seeks shelter from storms at Redwall Abbey, where a young mouse named Bisky tale-spins, telling the story of Prince Gonff stealing the titular Doomwyte Idol.<br /><br />However, Bisky has his share of critics including the squirrel Dwink, and meanwhile, two rats named Slegg and Gridj trudge through the stormy weather to the shoreline. Several other of the good creatures are quickly introduced, such as the dormouse Glisam, Father Abbot of Redwall, the squirrel Herbalist Torilis, the head cook mole Friar Skurpul, and the elderly mouse Samolus. At this time, Griv meets the leader of the carrion crows, Veeku. Back at the Abbey, the Redwallers peruse old texts such as Gonff’s diaries, curious as to what Wyte means in the first place.<br /><br />Other villains are exposed, such as ravens and reptiles such as snakes, with one of the chief serpents, Sicariss, supposedly having the blood of Asmodeus. Laird Bosie McScutta of Bowlaynee serves as Abbey Warrior, with fights against vermin such as the Painted Ones erupting, and younger Redwallers being kidnapped by them. The story satisfactorily resolves, with Doomwyte overall being another enjoyable yarn of Redwall, although like its predecessors it depicts specific animals in black and white terms, with creatures such as mice, squirrels, and moles being “good,” while rats, reptiles, and ravens are “bad.”<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10541106933928877581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3592132941?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elsa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elsa" href="/user/show/2478168-elsa">Elsa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3592132941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3621432798921755164">This one was much more satisfying than most late entries to the series. Jacques calls back to places and characters from the very early books--it examines the descendants of Gonff the Prince of Mousethieves, one of the groups of adversaries are the Painted Ones, and we encounter one of the line of Asmodeus.<br/><br/>Did Brian Jacques know this would be his last book (not published posthumously)? The Recorder's Epilogue reads in part:<br/>Lessons of truth and honesty<br/>From creatures, far more bold than me.<br/>I tried</span>
  <span id="freeText3621432798921755164" style="display:none">This one was much more satisfying than most late entries to the series. Jacques calls back to places and characters from the very early books--it examines the descendants of Gonff the Prince of Mousethieves, one of the groups of adversaries are the Painted Ones, and we encounter one of the line of Asmodeus.<br /><br />Did Brian Jacques know this would be his last book (not published posthumously)? The Recorder's Epilogue reads in part:<br />Lessons of truth and honesty<br />From creatures, far more bold than me.<br />I tried my best and played my part<br />To be amongst the brave of heart.<br />Mayhaps I failed, but now it seems<br />That I've become the Teller of Tales,<br />The scribe, the Weaver of Dreams. <br />A little acknowledgement of the author's role and of his intentions for his stories?<br /><br />This story suffers as it goes on from some serious character creep. There's a squirrel, a young mouse, an old mouse, a young hedgehog, an old hedgehog, a dormouse, two foremole, another mole, a otter Skipper, another otter, another young mouse, another old mouse, a hare, a Logalog, another shrew, another young squirrel, an owl... Nothing out of the ordinary for Redwall, but I've been listening to Redwall (the book) on audio, and those original stories were much tighter, with more well developed characters. Doomwytes felt like it might be that way; the first book and a half or so are darker than the usual and the small group of main characters get a more thorough development, but once the cast of thousands starts piling in, the book loses focus. It feels like a lot of thought went into the premise and establishing the conflict. But when it comes time to start resolving the various plot threads, Jacques falls back on his old tricks, and unfortunately only one of them feels like a deliberate callback to previous events.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3621432798921755164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11407474442548042193" style="display:none"> This book is different then other Redwall books. In most, the Abbey or some of their friends are under attack from evil vermin. In this book, the Redwallers discover one of their founders, Gonff, Prince of all Mousethieves, stole the jewel eyes from a statue of a crow because he couldn't save the lives of some shrews. Lady Columbine decides the stones are cursed so Gonff hides them with a bunch of clues, so of course the current Redwallers decide they have to find the jewels.<br /> By shear luck Korvus Skurr, the ruler of the doomwyte crows finds out a creature from Redwall has the jewels from his statue and he wants them back. While he does send come of his birds and a blind adder to capture a Redwaller so he can find out where his jewels are, Korvus spends most of his time in his cave feeding his fish. <br /> More confrontations are instigated by the Redwallers than the varuious bad guys throughout the story. There are many deaths in this book (like many Redwall books) but it was all to find jewels that Redwallers have no use for and don't place any value on.   <span id="freeText3745682920115856544" style="display:none"> Disappointingly not up to Jacques' usual standard, Doomwyte was a typical Redwall book. Too typical, in fact. The characters were so typically Redwall that they lacked personalities of their own. Owing to this I was a third of the way through the book before I cared much about any of them and two thirds through before I was interested in finishing it. There was also a lack of actual conflict between the two sides, making the scenes about the Wytes often seem irrelevant. Despite this, it did have the riddles and songs and food and friendship which I've always enjoyed in Redwall, and a good epilogue.</span>

<div id="review_1934236286" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1934236286" />
    <a title="Martina Sanjaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/918505-martina-sanjaya"><img alt="Martina Sanjaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471541383p2/918505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1934236286?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Martina Sanjaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Martina Sanjaya" href="/user/show/918505-martina-sanjaya">Martina Sanjaya</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1934236286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16957560413770585715">Reading Redwall series gives you something constant to expect, yet sometimes there were some surprises also. In this book there were some supposedly good creatures gone bad, but good for the story, methinks. Teaching children there're no absolute good and bad people, so keep 'em on their toes, wot? :)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2196081448" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2196081448" />
    <a title="Matthew McAndrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74161705-matthew-mcandrew"><img alt="Matthew McAndrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511568751p2/74161705.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2196081448?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew McAndrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew McAndrew" href="/user/show/74161705-matthew-mcandrew">Matthew McAndrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2196081448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9690284406065200124">This one felt like a Redwall, book 1 look-alike to me--not that that's a bad thing, except that I didn't feel like it added anything fresh to the series. Despite that one nitpick, the book was fun and the pages still turned themselves, like they always do with Brian Jacques' writing. I liked all the mystery involved. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2251225488" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2251225488" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3343384-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2251225488?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/3343384-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3343384-barbara?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2251225488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10840458962140867517">I do enjoy a good Redwall read. I forgot how pleasant Brian Jacques books are to read. I especially enjoy the ones set at Redwall Abbey. The Abbeybeasts have such a good time together in feasting and in rousting. The descriptions of the preparation of foodstuffs they partake of at their feasts are particularly entertaining. Fun, fun book!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3241788248" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3241788248" />
    <a title="Angel Clare" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111775989-angel-clare"><img alt="Angel Clare" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584901004p2/111775989.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3241788248?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angel Clare" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angel Clare" href="/user/show/111775989-angel-clare">Angel Clare</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142418536" href="/book/show/9045961-doomwyte">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3241788248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9878886306117483813">Fails to provide a unique protagonist or an involved antagonist, instead unwinding an only marginally engaging tale that is spread across a number of individual narratives. A few casually gruesome deaths and surprisingly poor grammar are the only truly negative elements of an otherwise decent, but unremarkable, tale.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+jqCwIG83ysLLI4pwVB2hB6tdXXoRuG7OkTYVZhdHa4fMzyy3djbuCu11eqrKezg9crC26UsvcViSXoBfuhqww==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X5HbBuUqUZgPlE5Am1ZKVbfQJZUymRrpf9nB8s9MtuW6mGV0uU5VCy8NFYPxL9AxXLeSO3/zRpcn1GOmKfnBiA==')})
  }

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12523033-la-educaci-n-de-henry-adams"><img alt="La educación de Henry Adams" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1407624696l/12523033._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>


<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_12523033'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12523033-la-educaci-n-de-henry-adams?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">La educación de Henry Adams<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/20404.Henry_Adams?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Henry Adams<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.65 avg rating &mdash; 3,298 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1918\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer5286686740845011173\">La educación de Henry Adams (1907), recientemente elegida por el consejo de la prestigiosa Modern Library como «la mejor obra de no ficción en lengua inglesa del siglo XX», es la atípica y personalísima autobiografía de un hombre que perteneció a una<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5286686740845011173\" style=\"display:none\">La educación de Henry Adams (1907), recientemente elegida por el consejo de la prestigiosa Modern Library como «la mejor obra de no ficción en lengua inglesa del siglo XX», es la atípica y personalísima autobiografía de un hombre que perteneció a una de las más ilustres familias del patriciado político norteamericano. Biznieto del segundo presidente de la Unión, nieto del sexto, hijo de un congresista y diplomático, Henry Adams nació bostoniano y abolicionista; fue testigo de excepción de acontecimientos decisivos como la Guerra de Secesión, el asesinato de Lincoln o la expansión del ferrocarril; conoció una larga serie de presidentes, de Zachary Taylor a Theodore Roosevelt; y vio, en fin, cómo Estados Unidos dejaba de ser un remoto vástago del puritanismo del siglo XVII y de la Revolución del XVIII para convertirse en una gran potencia mundial del siglo XX. Además de un original estudio sobre la evolución histórica de la sociedad, basado en los principios de la dinámica –masa y energía, fuerza e inercia, atracción y repulsión–, este libro es, ante todo, una búsqueda de la verdad y de un sistema de conocimiento, «el relato de una educación». De hecho, «a la persona o personas que figuran en él se les asignan valores sólo como educadores o educados». Pero, si la reflexión histórica parece concluir en el reconocimiento de una «perpetua victoria de los principios de la libertad y su conversión perpetua en principios del poder», el relato de formación se desarrolla en un mundo sin maestros, casi siempre «necio e ignorante», y que anima tan sólo a «la Persecución de la Ignorancia en Silencio». De una «inmitigable negrura», como dijo Henry James, incisiva cuando no corrosiva, brillante, sutil y radical en pensamiento y estilo. La educación de Henry Adams no es sólo un testimonio privilegiado sino una pieza clave de la literatura moderna.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"5286686740845011173\" href=\"#\" <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6096821031629684493"> Brian Jacques (pronounced 'jakes') was born in Liverpool, England on June 15th, 1939. Along with forty percent of the population of Liverpool, his ancestral roots are in Ireland, County Cork to be exact.<br/><br/>Brian grew up in the area around the Liverpool docks, where he attended St. John's School, an inner city school featuring a playground on its roof. At the age of ten, his very first day at St. Joh</span>
  <span id="freeText6096821031629684493" style="display:none"> Brian Jacques (pronounced 'jakes') was born in Liverpool, England on June 15th, 1939. Along with forty percent of the population of Liverpool, his ancestral roots are in Ireland, County Cork to be exact.<br /><br />Brian grew up in the area around the Liverpool docks, where he attended St. John's School, an inner city school featuring a playground on its roof. At the age of ten, his very first day at St. John's foreshadowed his future career as an author; given an assignment to write a story about animals, he wrote a short story about a bird who cleaned a crocodile's teeth. Brian's teacher could not, and would not believe that a ten year old could write so well. When young Brian refused to falsely say that he had copied the story, he was caned as "a liar". He had always loved to write, but it was only then that he realized he had a talent for it.<br />He wrote Redwall for the children at the Royal Wavertree School for the Blind in Liverpool, where as a truck driver, he delivered milk. Because of the nature of his first audience, he made his style of writing as descriptive as possible, painting pictures with words so that the schoolchildren could see them in their imaginations. He remained a patron of the school until his death.<br /><br />Brian lived in Liverpool, where his two grown sons, Marc, a carpenter and bricklayer, and David, a professor of Art and a muralist, still reside. David Jacques' work can be seen in Children's hospitals, soccer stadiums, and trade union offices as far away as Germany, Mexico, and Chile (not to mention Brian's photo featured in most of his books).<br /><br />Brian also ran a weekly radio show on BBC Radio Merseyside, until October 2006, where he shared his comedy and wit, and played his favourites from the world of opera - he was a veritable expert on The Three Tenors.<br /><br />When he was wasn't writing, Brian enjoyed walking his dog 'Teddy', a white West Highland Terrier, and completing crossword puzzles. When he found time he read the works of Mario Puzo, Damon Runyon, Richard Condon, Larry McMurty, and P.G. Wodehouse. He was also known to cook an impressive version of his favourite dish, spaghetti and meatballs.<br /><br />Sadly, Brian passed away on the 5th February 2011. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6096821031629684493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
